6. Note the following in read-actual data. I am not sure when I wrote it:
        !why is this age<agestart-1 and not age<agestart
        !because for ed, agestart is 22 in sim the initial conditions are assigned to age 21 and then 
        !the move rates at age 21 for ed people in sim turn out to be very large because they move immediately from their starting 
        !home location to the best uloc location. In the data, this moment is not there because of the setting of dat=ones 
        !for ages age<agestart. In order to let the estimation to its thing and be able to compare that large sim moving rate 
        !at age 21 to the data, I am setting the dat to ones for ages 0-20 rather than 0-21. doing this is also more consistent because 
        !now (i.e. when age<agestart case) the simulation has age 21 for the ed people but not the data. 
        !I am not doing this for noed though since for noed people there is no age read from the data that is less than mna

WOULDN'T THIS ALSO BE A PROBLEM FOR NOED THOUGH? I DON'T GET IT

I figured it out. it's just that when their mumar is so high, they don't have enough to make the transfers to divy up that large surplus anymore     STAR INSIGHT

when mumar increases too muhc they start falling, whcih makes sense that pattern

  011219

don't think onthejob search is good. because wages increase due to epsilons (when they get an offer during job and hcange to another one) as well as experience. 
and we don't observe experience nor job-to-job transitions. so can't tell the two apart. 
so I am getting rid of on the job search at least partially. 
see ahu jan19 011219 changes
now when onthejobsearch is set to FALSE, the onnly way wages changes within a location  adn cnditional on ee is through experience 
when moving it's both, but then we observe whether they are moving so it's better this way 
they can still get laid off and the probability of getting laid off is the same




  added initiation to getmom and objf


with no ojt then wages don't increase at all
which means that before (i.e. with ojt) all increase was coming from ojt rather than experience

AND THEN WDIF EUE S AND EUE M WERE ALWAYS TOO NEGATIVE AND LOW. 
I WAS THINKING THAT THAT EUE S CONSISTS OF BASICALLY JUST SIGMA STUFF BUT THIS IS WRONG. IT CONSITS OF SIGMA AND EXPERIENCE LOSS STUFF 
EUE M CONSISTS OF SIGMA AND LOC AND EXPERIENCE LOSS STUFF 
WHY IS WDIF FOR EE STAY AND ESPECIALLY EE MOVE ALWAYS SO HIGH?
BECAUSE THE ESTIMATION USUALLY GOES TO A HIGH ALF12 OR PRH POINT TO GET THE WAGE PROFILE CORRECTLY
THEN IF NOT FOR EXPERIENCE COEFFICIENT OR PRH, HOW DO I GET THE WAGE PROFILE RIGHT WITHOUT MESSING WDIF? 
I DON'T KNOW 

WHY IS WDIF EUE S AND EUE M ALWAYS SO NEGATIVE AND LOW? 
BECAUSE AGAIN, THE EPXERIENCE COEFFICIENT ALF12 OR PRH IS TOO HGIH. NOTE THAT EUE ALSO CONSISTS OF EXPERIENCE LOSS POTENTIALLY SO THE NEGATIVE COMES FROM THAT
IN FACT WHEN I DECREASE ALF12 OR PSIH 2 OR WHEN I DECREASE PROBLOSS, THEN THIS IS NOT THE CASE ANYMORE. SEE BELOW. 

BUT THEN AGAIN I ASK: HOW DO I CORRECT THOSE WDIF EE AND EUE THINGS WHILE ALSO GETTING THE WAGE PROFILE CORRRECT? 

AND ALSO HOW DO I IDENTIFY SEPARATELY PSIH AND ALF12? 
IF YOU GET RID OF THE GOING DOWN PART OF PSIH, THEN EUE WILL GIVE YOU ONLY SIGMA AND EE WILL GIVE YOU SIGMA PLUS EXPERIENCE 
BUT FOR EXPERIENCE IT WILL BE PSIH*ALF12 SO I DONT KNOW HOW TO SEPARATELY GET THOSE 
I GUESS I ALSO HAVE TO DO WDIF EE SQUARED? BECAUSE THAT WOUDL DIFFERENTIATE BETWEEN HIGH PRH/LOW ALF12 AND LOW PRH/HIGH ALF12 SCENARIOS. IS THIS RIGHT? IT SEEMS TO BE.

IF I INCREASE THE EXPERIENCE PART, THEN WDIF EE IS TOO HIGH
BUT NOTE THAT IT IS MAINLY WDIF MOVE THAT GOES UP TOO HIGH 
WDIF STAY IS USUALLY OK
SO NO PROBLEM THERE?

WDIF MOVE BEING TOO HIGH MEANS EITHER THAT LOC DIFFERENCES ARE TOO HIGH OR THAT THE RESERVATION WAGE TO MOVE IS TOO HIGH

AFTER 15 YEARS I JUST FIGURED OUT THE MU OVER SIGMA SITUATION. 
SEE NOTES PLEASE. IT IS THAT IF YOU HAVE SIGMA TO BE NORMALIZED TO 1 THEN MU WILL BE ESTIMATED ACCORDINGLY. DEPENDING ON WHAT YOUR PROB IS. SO IF MU OVERF SIGMA IS ESTIMATED TO BE 0 THEN YOU'LL HAVE AN ESTIMATE OF MU=0. 
THAT WOULD HAPPEN WHEN THE PROB IS 0.5.
DEPENDING ON WHAT THAT PROB IS, MU WILL ADJUST ACCORDINGLY, GIVEN SIGMA IS 1. SO YOU WONT HAVE THIS SIGMA IS GOOD FOR NOTHING SITUATION AS YOU PREVIOUSLY RETARDEDLY THOUGHT. 


see below that when you have low uhome and high hgih high movecosts, things don't work out. high move rates at 17 and then very low after that and very low homemove rates. 
so separately identified they are.

are they are they are they 




Below is ecst and sigo changing. 
As you can see the objval is very similar. The move rates do change quite a bit across both ecst as well as sigo
but the overall objval does not change 
For example, 3 and 8 are almost exactly similar in terms of almost all moments
3 is ecst=-6000 and sigo=0
8 is ecst=-9000 and sigo=3000
They are similar in terms of almost all moments except for a big difference in eu move moments (see below)
so you could say they are not separately identified except for the eu move moments so if there was more weight on it then maybe they would be sep identified? 

But I think that it's better to just not iterate on any movecost (ecst etc. also) and shut it down because as you can see from below, they don't seem to be strongly separately ident
except for the eu move situation 

So then no more movecost (ecst etc. also) 
Only iterate on sigo
What value should sigo be? 
When sigo is 6000, eu move looks low enough

When it was onlt the layoff rate that increased, the ee move decreased considerably. 
Which to me did not make sense. 
It turns out it was because of hte following:  
When they get laidoff, they are more likely to move that period. And when that happens, the moments counted them as employed move: 
t --- get laid off so that your employment next period is unemployed but at t your employment is still employed
      choose to move 
t+1 --- you are in a different location and you are unemployed

so then the above counted as e to u move i.e.  u|e move. 
so that e|e move is lower and u|e move is higher. 

To prevent this kind of accounting in the calculation of moments, I now added a restriction to ch array so that when they 
get laid off, they cannot choose anything other than staying put and staying uneployed for a period. 

In order to do this, I had to change getdec_s in order to add ch there. 
see getdec_s_old for the old version. 

Once I did this, then I no longer had the e|e move decrease a lot with small layoff rate changes
